<div id="review_2254725054" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2254725054" />
    <a title="Michael Finocchiaro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48483884-michael-finocchiaro"><img alt="Michael Finocchiaro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576692048p2/48483884.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2254725054?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Finocchiaro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Finocchiaro" href="/user/show/48483884-michael-finocchiaro">Michael Finocchiaro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48483884-michael-finocchiaro?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48483884-michael-finocchiaro?shelf=american-21st-c">american-21st-c</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48483884-michael-finocchiaro?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48483884-michael-finocchiaro?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48483884-michael-finocchiaro?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48483884-michael-finocchiaro?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2254725054" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6631427770433975379">The final volume of the Silo Trilogy picks up where the first one, Wool, left off. Having read Wool months before Dust, I have to admit that some of the characters and situations were a bit dusty in my mind, but still the narrative does stick together. Having learned of the nanobots in Shift and the apocalyptic plans of Thurman and his two ill-fated pals, it was interesting to see how Howey threaded the end of his story. I feel that the character development was always a little week in this tril</span>
  <span id="freeText6631427770433975379" style="display:none">The final volume of the Silo Trilogy picks up where the first one, Wool, left off. Having read Wool months before Dust, I have to admit that some of the characters and situations were a bit dusty in my mind, but still the narrative does stick together. Having learned of the nanobots in Shift and the apocalyptic plans of Thurman and his two ill-fated pals, it was interesting to see how Howey threaded the end of his story. I feel that the character development was always a little week in this trilogy - what supports the books is really the plot and action more than the characters in my humble opinion. <br /><br />As for the entire trilogy, it has been compared favorably to Hunger Games. Having read that one last year, I'd say this one is for older kids than Hunger Games was (more sex and language here), but that the character development of Katniss was probably more interesting than that of Charlotte or Juliette or Solo or Donald in Dust. I guess that is somewhat to be expected since the Solo series takes place over a much longer period of time. The future that Howey projects is even more dire and hopeless than that of HG. At the risk of a spoiler, I just don't find it logical that only two live and one dead silo out of fifty would be the subject here. I would have expected more of the silos to be in communication and certainly also to overcome the various safeguards keeping them from "outside". There were other things I found improbable where my suspension of disbelief was pushed a little too far (like how did they populate the silos with 1000s of people without anyone figuring out the bigger picture? How could Thurman have built 50 silos rather than just one?). <br /><br />So, if you are not a stickler for realism and want pure escapism and are not too fussy about character development, you may enjoy this series. I found it fun and thought-provoking but inferior to other dystopian classics such as, say, The Handmaid's Tale or Brave New World.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6631427770433975379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2191822077" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2191822077" />
    <a title="Adam Goldfarb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57496994-adam-goldfarb"><img alt="Adam Goldfarb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468021951p2/57496994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2191822077?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adam Goldfarb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adam Goldfarb" href="/user/show/57496994-adam-goldfarb">Adam Goldfarb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2191822077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6868401484584259531">This was an absolute disappointment. I was going to give it two stars but after the long infuriating trek through this mess of a conclusion I just can’t bring myself to give it more than one. <br/><br/>I feel badly being negative but this is just deserving of it. Shift had such promise of what was to come. It built up my expectations to a conclusion of hope and these characters who were finally developed after a weak origin in Wool would finally come into their own. <br/><br/>Instead I was given characters who were</span>
  <span id="freeText6868401484584259531" style="display:none">This was an absolute disappointment. I was going to give it two stars but after the long infuriating trek through this mess of a conclusion I just can’t bring myself to give it more than one. <br /><br />I feel badly being negative but this is just deserving of it. Shift had such promise of what was to come. It built up my expectations to a conclusion of hope and these characters who were finally developed after a weak origin in Wool would finally come into their own. <br /><br />Instead I was given characters who were absolute idiots and could never understand what is in their own best interest. The whole premise of this story was that a group of people hit the reset button on humanity because we had gotten out of control and lapsed into nothing but destruction. Putting survivors underground to rebuild for hundreds of years so that perhaps we could become better. <br /><br />What we have is not only a complete failure of this plan a sacrifice but we have survivors who should not have been the ones to succeed because they represent the worst of us. The “heroes” constantly make things worse for the people they try to help because of their own egos, selfishness and drive for revenge. <br /><br />Wool set the world, Shift clarified it and gave us hope, and Dust did what the title promises...took this series with such potential and turned it into a disappointing dust from which nothing will ever grow. <br /><br />In fiction we are given the opportunity to create worlds and universes that are better than our own. Reading is an escape into places we wish to one day be able to visit, rescue, or even destroy. But here we are given our own world that has no hope. The best of us die, the worst of us live, and we are doomed to live in this cycle of disappointment and misery for all eternity. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6868401484584259531" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_718780904" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/718780904" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/718780904?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=decent-secondary-characters">decent-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=liked-the-world">liked-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer718780904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8399600041503115429"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>Not as engrossing as <i>Wool</i> or <i>Shift</i> — the plot, the mystery, the characters, and the relationships lost most of their appeal, they just didn't captivate me like they did in the previous two books. I have to say, <i>Dust</i> was mostly disappointing — I didn't hate it, I actually quite liked a lot of things, but overall it didn't meet my expectations.<br/><br/>-The first half was rather dull, nothing much seemed to happen. Juliette's mission to dig to Silo 17 dragged on for ages, and Donald + Charlotte's a</span>
  <span id="freeText8399600041503115429" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />Not as engrossing as <i>Wool</i> or <i>Shift</i> — the plot, the mystery, the characters, and the relationships lost most of their appeal, they just didn't captivate me like they did in the previous two books. I have to say, <i>Dust</i> was mostly disappointing — I didn't hate it, I actually quite liked a lot of things, but overall it didn't meet my expectations.<br /><br />-The first half was rather dull, nothing much seemed to happen. Juliette's mission to dig to Silo 17 dragged on for ages, and Donald + Charlotte's arc was rather slow moving. <br /><br />-The characters were a bit of a mixed bag. I hated the MC's (Juliette and Donald), the secondary characters were pretty good though. Lukas was okay, but I did find the way he constantly panted after Juliette annoying. Courtnee, Solo and Charlotte were likeable. Elise's POV was random, her puppy/paedo arc didn't really fit in with the rest of the story.<br /><br />-I was so sick of Juliette's selfish attitude, she didn't even attempt to do her job as the mayor even though she knew it would ease people's fears. I know she never wanted to be mayor but the fact that she was okay abusing her mayoral power… But at the same time refused to the required day-to-day responsibilities of the mayor pissed me off. She didn't want to help the people in her Silo, she just wanted to go off and do whatever crazy idea came into her head. I was glad that the Silo turned against her, she didn't deserve anyone's respect, she cared more about Silo 1 and 17 than the welfare of her own people.<br />I found Juliette's obsession with reaching Silo 17/Solo/the kids weird since she was so eager to leave them in the first book. It was like she wasn't happy no matter what circumstance she was in — when Silo 17 was eventually reached she quickly forgot about Solo and the kids (even though she was apparently so desperate to rescue them that she endangered thousands of people), and moved onto a shiny new project she started. She repeatedly put everyone's lives at risk just so she could satisfy her own curiousity. It was her fault that her Silo was shut down.<br /><br />-Charlotte was a decent character, but for the first half she didn't do much apart from worry about Donald's health, it was kind of boring. Her arc did get more interesting when Donald was taken by Thurman - her contacting Juliette, sneaking out, and meeting Darcy was pretty entertaining. I loved that she escaped Silo 1 and met up with Juliette, it made the end more hopeful since she knew about the old world and could pass on her knowledge to everyone that escaped.<br /><br />-How did Thurman survive breathing the air outside? Shouldn't the bad nanos outside have gotten into Thurman's body and attacked the good nanos? Did he have more powerful nanos or something? Or did he have medical treatment after 'saving' Donald? <br /><br />-I hated Anna in <i>Shift</i> but she wasn't nearly as bad as I initially thought. She was the first one to figure out Thurman's endgame, it was great how she turned her back on her dad and tried to save the other Silos. In the previous book, I thought she deserved being killed, but after reading <i>Dust</i> I really wish she'd survived.<br /><br />-What happened to the creepy congregation, Remmy, and Mr Rash? The disgusting paedos thought it was cool to marry off a seven year old to an old man. They should have all been killed off. That whole fucked up congregation came out of nowhere, I can't believe that they were so many people that were cool with the paedophilic marriage — especially when 1. Children were supposed to be rare and precious and 2. Marrying children off to adults was something that was never done before in the Silos. The whole arc was weird and random.<br /><br />-There were too many characters who I rooted for that ended up dead (Darcy, Marcus, Donald and Shirly). And some of the deaths seemed like they were written more for shock value than for anything else.<br /><br />-I was disappointed that Silo 1 was destroyed in such an unimaginative and simple way. I wanted there to be an epic battle between Juliette/Silo 18 and Silo 1/Thurman - instead Donald just blew up Silo 1. After all the manipulating, absolute power and knowledge of Silo 1, it was unimpressive that they were wiped out so easily. There should have been more complexity and intelligence to their destruction.<br /><br />All in all, <i>Dust</i> was mostly enjoyable but it wasn't quite as exciting as the first two books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8399600041503115429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_711666320" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/711666320" />
    <a title="Michael Long" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13385702-michael-long"><img alt="Michael Long" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379295045p2/13385702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/711666320?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Long" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Long" href="/user/show/13385702-michael-long">Michael Long</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13385702-michael-long?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer711666320" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17207798694441576036">DUST, the final book in the Silo saga brings an end to both the WOOL and SHIFT series. Want to know what happens with Juliette being mayor? What about Troy and Charlotte in silo 1? Will Troy's charade as Thurman go unnoticed? What is up with Troy's cough? Will Juliette be reunited with Solo and the kids in silo 17? Will silo 1 continue to put up with rebellion from silo 18? And what will silo 18 do with it's new found knowledge about the outside and other silos? What about the fate of all the ot</span>
  <span id="freeText17207798694441576036" style="display:none">DUST, the final book in the Silo saga brings an end to both the WOOL and SHIFT series. Want to know what happens with Juliette being mayor? What about Troy and Charlotte in silo 1? Will Troy's charade as Thurman go unnoticed? What is up with Troy's cough? Will Juliette be reunited with Solo and the kids in silo 17? Will silo 1 continue to put up with rebellion from silo 18? And what will silo 18 do with it's new found knowledge about the outside and other silos? What about the fate of all the other silos? What is that brief blue sky vision from the drone? Do the nanos continue to destroy the entire world? And just what is the end game that silo 1 has planned out? And finally, will these poor people ever make it out of the silo prisons? All of this is answered and more in the novel.<br /><br />If you've read the other books in this series, you have to get this one. There really isn't any reason not to. This book answers a ton of questions and wraps up the story nicely. It is full of action, with only a few slow sections that were more philosophical. The plot really is a roller coaster ride with ups and downs, and both smart and stupid decisions from characters we love. We see absolutely terrible decisions, but we also see sacrifice and heroism.<br /><br />And whereas the first Wool was all about cleaning those cameras...in this novel, nobody cares about those stupid cameras as there is way too much more important stuff going on. So read it, and find out what that stuff is!<br /><br />See my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.michaelscifan.us">http://www.michaelscifan.us</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17207798694441576036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8299690032737945606">4.5 stars...<br/><br/>I fell in love with the first book in this series, Wool, when I read it. It's one of my all time favorites. Then I read the second book, Shift, and hated it. It was written in a different style then Wool and it contained a lot of flashbacks to older times which didn't do anything for me at all. I wouldn't recommend skipping Shift though because you do get a lot of the backstory which you need to know to fully appreciate the whole story. I was hoping though, that Dust wouldn't be anyt</span>
  <span id="freeText8299690032737945606" style="display:none">4.5 stars...<br /><br />I fell in love with the first book in this series, Wool, when I read it. It's one of my all time favorites. Then I read the second book, Shift, and hated it. It was written in a different style then Wool and it contained a lot of flashbacks to older times which didn't do anything for me at all. I wouldn't recommend skipping Shift though because you do get a lot of the backstory which you need to know to fully appreciate the whole story. I was hoping though, that Dust wouldn't be anything like it and was written more like Wool and it was. : ) Yay! It started out where Wool left off so I took to it immediately and finished it the same day. What's really special about this series I think is the setting and the world building. How the society is structured within the Silos is just brilliant. I also really liked how Howey wrapped up the ending nice and neat so you weren't left with any cliffhangers or a thousand questions either. If you like dystopian books, then this series is a definite must-read!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_697625996" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/697625996" />
    <a title="Timothy Ward" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4867952-timothy-ward"><img alt="Timothy Ward" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319336249p2/4867952.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/697625996?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Timothy Ward" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Timothy Ward" href="/user/show/4867952-timothy-ward">Timothy Ward</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4867952-timothy-ward?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4867952-timothy-ward?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4867952-timothy-ward?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4867952-timothy-ward?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer697625996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16472993410268203675">Reviewed at <a href='http://www.sfsignal.com/archives/2014/10/book-review-dust-by-hugh-howey/' rel='nofollow noopener'>SF Signal</a><br/><br/>REVIEW SUMMARY: Satisfying conclusion to a remarkable science fiction series<br/><br/>MY RATING: 4.5 Stars<br/><br/>BRIEF SYNOPSIS: The end to a post-apocalyptic epic where people have survived underground in silos but are finally going to find out whether they can survive in the wasteland above.<br/><br/>MY REVIEW:<br/>PROS: Has the feel of a science fiction series we’ll tell our grandchildren about; shows improvement in pacing from previous books in series; surprise ending.<br/>CONS: Lacked enough surviving char</span>
  <span id="freeText16472993410268203675" style="display:none">Reviewed at <a href="http://www.sfsignal.com/archives/2014/10/book-review-dust-by-hugh-howey/" rel="nofollow noopener">SF Signal</a><br /><br />REVIEW SUMMARY: Satisfying conclusion to a remarkable science fiction series<br /><br />MY RATING: 4.5 Stars<br /><br />BRIEF SYNOPSIS: The end to a post-apocalyptic epic where people have survived underground in silos but are finally going to find out whether they can survive in the wasteland above.<br /><br />MY REVIEW:<br />PROS: Has the feel of a science fiction series we’ll tell our grandchildren about; shows improvement in pacing from previous books in series; surprise ending.<br />CONS: Lacked enough surviving characters to keep us as engaged as we were in earlier books of the series; subplot about the endangered child was not rewarding enough.<br /><br />Wool‘s first line, “The children were playing while Holston climbed to his death…” sets the reader of this series into a common frame of mind where happiness is outside one’s reach, but where the person experiencing that separation refuses to give up hope. There’s a reason why Mr. Howey often signs his books, “Dare to hope.” Holston is just one of many characters who come to realize, possibly too late, what really matters, and experience the force within that pushes us toward achieving happiness, even at great cost.<br /><br />As someone who has experienced depression, I know what it’s like to wonder where this force is that pushes me toward happiness; sometimes it feels like I’m less than those around me because that push is gone. Mr. Howey puts characters in places where they pass through whatever fog has kept them from experiencing this motivating force, and then we share their thrill as they run full-spirit ahead toward the embodiment of their hope.<br /><br />Some characters don’t make it, but the beauty of fiction is that we share their enthusiasm, and where they fail, we take the baton and continue the race, inspired by the heart-thumping emotions they evoked.<br /><br />This series started with a novelette called “Wool“, which the author has offered permanently free in eBook format. Have a peak and see for yourself how his characters will move you. I’m confident you’ll join me at the finish line of Dust‘s conclusion, eager to share the word for a long time how much you loved this series.<br /><br />It is interesting to see how the books differed. Wool remains my favorite. I read that so quickly and with such fascination and emotional tension that it will go down as one of my top three books. The middle lagged a little in the setup before the major conflict, but other than that it was flawless. The story was poetic, heart-wrenching and thrilling all in a fascinating underground dystopia. Shift, Book Two in the Silo Saga, started out strong and had some more powerfully emotional moments as our main character from the past dealt with career versus time with his wife, and didn’t realize what he was missing until it was too late. His fight to get her back tore my heart out and made me a better person. The second storyline of the porter was also a great and emotional experience within the silo culture, but the third storyline lagged a lot and the end was really hard to read through.<br /><br />With Dust, the pacing is even better than the previous two books. Our surviving main characters have the final task of escaping the silo and seeing what future can be had outside amidst the poisoned world. Finding out this secret is a terrific motivation to finish the series, as well as the surprises encountered in the book. The story flew by and I’m very happy with the ending. It’s truly a remarkable series. I only have two small complaints. First, because a lot of characters from the previous books died, it felt like I wasn’t as emotionally invested in the ones that survived. Second, and a very minor gripe, was the child-in-danger subplot. It wasn’t the most interesting or rewarding to read through. Other than that though, this series is a must-read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16472993410268203675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer993381195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8116445497800027092">4 Stars<br/><br/>Fascinating, intriguing and down right scary. Dust picks up where Wool left off. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Juliette returning from Silo 17, ready to save the people (kids) she found over there.  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/> Lots of themes played out with each of these books. Like another reviewer stated, <b>"With Wool, it was the stairs and a representation of class or hierarchy. With Shift, it was all about power and challenges to that power. In Dust, his theme is ‘making your actions count’."</b> I had never thought </span>
  <span id="freeText8116445497800027092" style="display:none">4 Stars<br /><br />Fascinating, intriguing and down right scary. Dust picks up where Wool left off. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Juliette returning from Silo 17, ready to save the people (kids) she found over there.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /> Lots of themes played out with each of these books. Like another reviewer stated, <b>"With Wool, it was the stairs and a representation of class or hierarchy. With Shift, it was all about power and challenges to that power. In Dust, his theme is ‘making your actions count’."</b> I had never thought about it like that before, but it makes perfect sense. It was also by design, as we find out towards the end. There were so many secrets revealed and such damaging secrets. Horrible, selfish secrets that became the doom of mankind and no apologies given. Only a megalomaniac could come up with this bull-ish. <br /><br />So, most questions are neatly answered by the end and some things are revealed that leave you angry, sad and bewildered that folks could come up with such a hellish idea. Even though there was a lot of info, the pacing was pretty quick and a little rushed at the end, but we are living on borrowed time people. We gotta move fast. I pray that SAND, another Hugh Howey novel, has nothing to do with Wool. I really want the nice, tidy bow ending. No matter how damaged and bloody it was by the end. <br /><br />Believe me, that was not a spoiler...…<br /><br />Edit: 11/22/18<br />Side note or P.S. or BTW: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ So, what is up with missing scars, birthmarks, etc., that Juliette mentioned??? Are they doing cryo on the other Silo's too??? Are they erasing memories with those pills or "dust??" I don't think that was addressed at the end. I think Juliette suspected something, but was under pressure to get everyone out, who wanted to leave. Another question; was the Dome she spoke of, just the actual dome of dust/debris/poison; or was that an actual dome?? Mmmmm. It read like it was just a dome of debris and poison, but everything is suspect in this damned book.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_697706784" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/697706784" />
    <a title="Ted Gault" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4306495-ted-gault"><img alt="Ted Gault" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492081971p2/4306495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/697706784?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ted Gault" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ted Gault" href="/user/show/4306495-ted-gault">Ted Gault</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer697706784" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3830052712045732351">To me, both Wool and Shift were easily 5 star books/collections. The combination of believable and likable characters, good tension and build up, and the slow and enticing unwinding of Howey's intriguing universe kept me entrapped from page to page. Unfortunately, I can't say the same for Dust. I don't know what went wrong, but I struggled to connect with the characters in the same way I had previously. Maybe it is because their development climaxed in Shift. Between Shift and Dust we see the ch</span>
  <span id="freeText3830052712045732351" style="display:none">To me, both Wool and Shift were easily 5 star books/collections. The combination of believable and likable characters, good tension and build up, and the slow and enticing unwinding of Howey's intriguing universe kept me entrapped from page to page. Unfortunately, I can't say the same for Dust. I don't know what went wrong, but I struggled to connect with the characters in the same way I had previously. Maybe it is because their development climaxed in Shift. Between Shift and Dust we see the characters largely (though not wholly) emerge from the inner struggles that defined them previously and instead find conflict inter rather than intra-personally. <br /><br />But more disappointingly, it seems that most of the discoveries of the Silo universe (or rather the discoveries Howey was willing to reveal) were already uncovered in the first two books. Although there is closure for some of the characters (in what I consider too predictable a conclusion), there was nothing substantively new revealed about the dynamics of the "dust" and its final impact on the world, the fate of the "lost" silos, or of the silos' engineering in general. On more minor notes, the ultimate outcome of one of the main silos is left in doubt and a subplot about a religious cult left noticeably underdeveloped. In sum, this book doesn't feel like a real conclusion. I'm sure this was Howey's intention as he leaves room for the wonderful fan fiction that has popped up around the trilogy. But as a huge fan of the Silo Saga, the author's own "ending" just doesn't do it for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3830052712045732351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/762705583?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arielle" href="/user/show/6762949-arielle">Arielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6762949-arielle?shelf=dystopia-and-post-apocalypse">dystopia-and-post-apocalypse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6762949-arielle?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer762705583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1735786175873930040">"She felt none of the fear from the last time she was sent out, but none of the deluded hope that drove many to exile. Somewhere between pointless dreams and hopeless dread was a desire to know the world, And, if possible, make it better." (page 113)<br/><br/><br/>Though Dust is largely plot-driven, it is worth mentioning that the writing itself, for all its lack of elegance or beauty, is certainly better than adequate. The characters actually have individual voices - something very rarely the case in stories </span>
  <span id="freeText1735786175873930040" style="display:none">"She felt none of the fear from the last time she was sent out, but none of the deluded hope that drove many to exile. Somewhere between pointless dreams and hopeless dread was a desire to know the world, And, if possible, make it better." (page 113)<br /><br /><br />Though Dust is largely plot-driven, it is worth mentioning that the writing itself, for all its lack of elegance or beauty, is certainly better than adequate. The characters actually have individual voices - something very rarely the case in stories with multiple viewpoints. Howey pulls together threads from both prequels in a tense and dramatic lead up to the grand finale of the series. <br /><br />I did find that having missed reading Shift I was left a little lost in the scenes with Charlotte and her brother - this is definitely not a novel that can be slipped into comfortably without prior knowledge of Howey’s post-apocalyptic world. It is, however, a decent conclusion to a very good trilogy, and one fans should be satisfied by.<br /><br /><a href="http://www.nzbooklovers.co.nz/science-fiction-fantasy/book-review-dust-by-hugh-howey/" rel="nofollow noopener">Full review here.</a><br /><br />*I received this book from the publisher for an honest review, through the NZ Booklovers website.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer547361825227950363">Oh yes! What a satisfying end to the enjoyably unique and imaginative Silo series. Would I prefer it to continue? Of course, but it's always best to leave them wanting more.<br/><br/>My only complaint, and I do mean "only", is that the Audible.com version uses a reader who pronounces the word "palm" so oddly I found myself giggling every time the word was used. It's not a word in too common usage in our current culture, most people preferring "hand" or "grasp", but it became laughably obvious it is one of</span>
  <span id="freeText547361825227950363" style="display:none">Oh yes! What a satisfying end to the enjoyably unique and imaginative Silo series. Would I prefer it to continue? Of course, but it's always best to leave them wanting more.<br /><br />My only complaint, and I do mean "only", is that the Audible.com version uses a reader who pronounces the word "palm" so oddly I found myself giggling every time the word was used. It's not a word in too common usage in our current culture, most people preferring "hand" or "grasp", but it became laughably obvious it is one of Howey's favorites, popping up frequently.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hVVbOhR+McfGKLaUW2qDliGXwaVxSXXyTbwAAznLJVYTlnPT+0PTOBlD5Fpil5Nva+F3OYMKtPzxv9cEQxG5OQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('L/SdgC18fIMcPsI7L1K+VaTJJP8uxf/iDyDbGbPCyLa5N7VpwkGefMNVkPUWr66s7r+SY9yGPuyzIwweyRhU2Q==')})
  }
